Side 10 af 41 
Perquisitions for structural analysis 
All elements are dimensioned and designed to carry 5 stories of concrete slabs including: imposed, live and 
natural loads as well as self-weight. Concrete slabs where used for the design, as concrete slabs are heavier 
than wooden slab elements. This ensures that the element can be used in all situations, both for new 
buildings, and as a substitute element in a renovation. All bamboo elements are calculated as if they were 
glue laminated timber, as no standards for bamboo structures are available and certified yet.  
Beams 
The beam is dimensioned to be 140 mm x 60 mm and spans over a length of 2.4 meter. The beams in one 
element spans over five columns which the it distributes the loads to. 
The beams are subjected to loads from 
 
Elements above beam 
 
Imposed and live loads 
 
Nature loads 
 
Self-weight 
Beams are calculated for both roof slab and indoor slab, as the load combinations for each scenario gives 
different load sizes. Beams are calculated as simply supported beams, spanning between two columns with 
0.6 meters between.  
Moment capacity 
The beams moment capacity was calculated based on the design bending strength fm,d. Each beam was 
designed based on the maximum moment, which creates stress in the cross-section area. The stresses from 
the moment are designed to be lower than the bending strength of the element. Each beam was design for 
different load cases, as wood structures normally is. The beams are designed based on the maximum of the 
P-, M- and K-load.

8 ∙𝑝∙𝐿ଶ

𝑈= 𝜎௠

The beams are design so that the utilization is less than 100% of the beam’s capacity, to ensure that the 
beam can handle the stresses.

The designed deflection is designed to be less than the allowable deflection for the beam. Eb is assumed the 
same as Em and Gm is assumed based on the highest strength laminated timber.  
Columns 
The column is dimensioned to be 50 mm x 140 mm and spans over a length of 3 meter. 
The columns are subjected to loads from: 
 
Elements above column 
 
Imposed and live loads 
 
Nature loads 
 
Self-weight 
 
Moment from façade  
The vertical loads working on the columns includes the loads from elements above, slabs and walls including 
imposed and live loads. Besides from the vertical loads, horizontal loads from wind acts on the structure, 
both as pressure and suction. The most critical load scenario taken the moment of the eccentricities of the 
elements and façade into account with suction from the wind, as well as an outer eccentricity from the 
placement of the slab on the element. This scenario creates the larges outwards moment and is thereby the 
dimensional scenario, as the wind load in pressure would only benefit the load bearing capacity of the 
element.  
 
 
 
The columns are designed as simply supported. 
The load bearing capacity was determined based on the following calculations.

Maximum allowable deflection for characteristic wind load is: L/250 [2] 
Trusses 
In order to stabilize the walls against the wind pressure and suction, wind trusses are implemented into the 
structure. The trusses are designed for the wind load, W.k, on a corner, with a load width of 2,7 meter (half 
the length of one slab element).  When the windload hits “Façade A”, “façade B” must stabilize the wall, 
which the truss is designed to do.

U-VALUE CALCULATION OF PREFABRICATED WALL ELEMENT 
Unidimensional U-Value Calculation 
 
In this section the unidimensional calculation of the U-value for the different wall layouts is presented. 
The calculation was performed by applying the following formula: 
𝑈=
1
𝑅𝑠𝑜+ 𝑅1 + 𝑅2 + 𝑅3 + 𝑅𝑛+ 𝑅𝑠𝑖
 
Where R is the resistivity of each wall layer calculated as R= l/lambda [m^2K/W] (lambda is the thermal 
conductivity and l the thickness of the layer), 1 to n indicate the layers of the wall, Rsi and Rso indicate 
the fixed internal and external resistance. 
The materials properties for the calculation were all taken from the chosen product’s technical sheets, 
this were provided by the company CalceCanapa®.

Glaser Method Calculations 
Input Data 
The three main parameters needed to perform the Glaser calculation are the thicknesses of the different wall 
layers, the thermal conductivity and the vapour permeability of the material. The following table summarizes 
the used parameters.

Calculation Method 
The Glaser method calculates and assesses the moisture transport in a building component by considering the 
vapour diffusion throughout its layers. The amount of possible interstitial condensation for the winter month 
can be calculated and it can be assessed whether this dries out fast during the summer month.  
In this section the two used tools are shown which were used to perform the calculation. The first one is the 
table used to calculate amount of water that flows through the wall in the dry out period, this is needed in the 
month when no condensation occurs and the amount of vapour flows out of the wall (dry out in summer). The 
second tool is the one used two calculate the amount of interstitial condensation when it occurs in the winter 
months.  
Both calculation methods calculate the temperature and vapour pressure profiles of the cross section. When 
the vapour pressure exceeds the saturated vapour pressure for the calculated temperature, condensation 
occurs. In this case the vapour pressure profile needs to be adjusted as when it exceeds the saturated vapour 
pressure it needs to be replaced with this one (relative humidity can not be higher than 100%), then the amount 
of condensed water can be calculated.  
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
166
Prefabricated wall element with hemp and bamboo
==PAGE:177==
3 
 
Calculation table in case no condensation occurs, wall layout 2.2 in the month of October is presented in the 
example.

==PAGE:178==

Calculation table in case condensation occurs, wall layout 2.1 in the month of January is presented in the 
example. The first is the table that indicates the condensation point. The second one is where the vapour 
pressure profile is adjusted and the amount of condensed water is calculated.

Input data and results of WUFI Pro Simulations 
In this section the input material data and climate files are presented as well as the main graphs from the most 
significant simulation in WUFI Pro. The graphs show total water content and water content in each layer, 
temperature-relative humidity graphs and temperature-moisture diagram. With this all the evaluation 
summarized in the report can be demonstrated and assessed.  
Material data 
The following tables and graphs show the material properties of the four materials used for the different wall 
layouts in the best simulation. The data was taken from the Calcecanapa® product sheets for what concerns bulk 
density, specific heat capacity, thermal conductivity and water vapour diffusion factor. The missing data 
(porosity and  sorption curves) was researched in literature (Transient hygrothermal behaviour of Lime-Hemp 
Materials, Arnaud Evrard, 2008) or taken from similar materials in the WUFI Pro material database, when 
analogies were possible. Some assessed plasters were taken directly from the WUFI Pro material data base.

Climate data 
In this section the used climate files are quickly presented. the outdoor climates are chosen from the climate 
map in WUFI Pro. Lund was chosen because it is the closest available to Copenhagen, while Marseille was chosen 
to assess a Mediterranean climate. For the indoor climate three options are offered by the program: climate 
conditions from the European EN 15026 standards, the international ISO 13788 standards and the ASHRAE 160 
standards. All three concern hygrothermal evaluation of building components. For Lund the ISO 13788 was 
chosen because it was the worst performing one as the internal temperature is set two 20°C and therefore has 
the smallest summer dry out potential. For Marseille the AHRAE 160 was chosen as it had the hottest internal 
Prefabricated wall element with hemp and bamboo
175
==PAGE:186==
12 
 
temperatures and quite high internal relative humidity levels: the worst case for a hot climate was considered 
(no air conditioning and so on).

Evaluation criteria of the simulations 
The following list summarizes the used evaluation criteria to interpret the performed simulations :  
• 
Total water content of the wall, the amount and if in the years it stabilizes on a constant value, 
otherwise it means that the wall is soaking up water throughout time. 
• 
Water content in each layer, if this oversteps certain limits it could deteriorate the material and affect 
its properties. No specific recommended water content levels were found for the accessed materials, 
but to prevent rot in organic materials such as wood, or natural fibres the water content should not 
exceed 20-25 mass-percent over long periods of time. The standard considers a safety margin as 
wood rot fungi start the decomposing process with a moisture content of 25-30 mass-percent. 
• 
The relative humidity in certain monitoring points in the wall. In permeable materials there is a 
gradual transition between sorption moisture and dew water, therefore it is not possible to identify a 
specific amount of condensation water. Anyhow if RH is close to 100% free saturation condition is 
reached, which means a large amount of water was transported to the assessed point, this on the 
long term could have negative effects on the material. 
• 
Effects of driving rain. 
• 
Possible mould growth on indoor surface, by looking at the temperature-moisture diagrams and the 
limiting curves LIM B I and LIM B II. 
• 
Loss of thermal insulation capacity (thermal conductivity increasing with moisture contents) 
• 
Cohesion between materials 
The evaluation criteria are taken from [WUFI Pro.Analysis, interpretation and assessment of the calculation 
results. 2018.URL:https://www.wufi-forum.com/viewtopic.php?t=1623]

Only this two summarising cross section are presented for the simulations in Marseille. In overall the wall is 
performing better in Mediterranean climate than in Scandinavian one.  As it can be seen in the figures the 
external hempcrete plate is not completely wet and the insulation never reaches the 100% of relative humidity. 
In this case the main driving rain comes from south east, therefore again the north facing façade performs in 
general better than the south one, but in this case no constant increasing of the total water content is happening. 
• 
Total water content: varies constantly in time between 12 and 24 kg/m2 for the south facing wall and 
between 11 and 18 kg/m2 for the south facing one 
• 
Water content in external Hempcrete plate: the water content in the external south facing plate is 
still too high as it reaches peaks of 37 mass percentage (the limit is set to 25-28%), which on the long 
term could affect the material and its properties. The north one instead is ok, as only mass 
percentage of 20% is reached. 
• 
Water content in hemp fibre plate: the water content in the hemp fibre is in both cases acceptable. 
• 
Water content in internal Hempcrete plate and internal insulation: also in this materials for both the 
north and south facing walls the water content is acceptable. 
• 
Relative humidity in monitoring point A: In winter the RH reaches 100% a few times but in overall it 
fluctuates between 85 and 95% for south and 70 and 95% for the north. This values enter in an 
acceptable range, as water probably does not accumulate excessively. 
• 
Relative humidity in monitoring point B and C: In this monitoring points, the relative humidity is less 
worrying than the levels assessed in the walls located in Lund, as in winter it peaks at 94% in the 
south facing wall and at 85% for the north facing one.  
• 
Temperature-moisture diagrams with limiting curves LIM B I and LIM B II, mould on internal 
surface: no risk of mould growth on the internal surface of the wall

FINAL PREFABRICATED WALL DESIGN 
This is the final designed layout of the wall, only the simulation for the south facing wall located in Lund will be 
presented. This because it is the closest simulation for a possible wall element installed in Copenhagen and 
furthermore it is the worst case scenario of the assessed one. Anyhow the results are very similar to the one of 
wall layout 4, therefore the same conclusions can be drawn. The final design was assessed to see if additional 
issues due to the optimization process would appear. 
 
 
 
Total water content: 
 
A 
B 
C 
 
-vPanel glue 
202
Prefabricated wall element with hemp and bamboo
==PAGE:213==
39 
 
The average total water amount in this wall layout gets constant in time while decreasing, which is a good sign 
as the wall gets dryer. 
Water content in exterior plaster: 
 
This layer has a very similar water content compared to the other wall layouts. This because it is actually the 
same external finish, therefore it absorbs the same amount of water. 
Water content in external insulation panels: 
 
The water content in this layer is slightly higher compared to the one of wall layout 4. This is because the panel 
glue which was inserted in this simulation, blocks the moisture flow through out the wall as it has a very different 
vapour permeability compared both the hemp fibres and the hempcrete. As seen already in other assessments 
it is important to combine materials next to each other with a similar vapour permeability. Anyhow the insulation 
system offered by the company Calcecanapa is designed in this way and the assessed different does not make a 
big different on the final conclusions. The water content is slightly to high but the issue needs to be solved with 
a less water absorbing finishing layer. 
Prefabricated wall element with hemp and bamboo

==PAGE:214==

The water content in the Hempcrete plate is definitively acceptable and is very similar to all the other assessed 
cases. This is a good sign especially because the bamboo load-bearing structure is not affected by moisture. 
Furthermore the hempcrete plate will not lose its insulating capacities.  
 
Relative humidity in monitoring point A: 
 
Relative humidity is similar to the one of wall layout 4, even though it has higher peaks in summer. In general a 
insulation panel with higher density could improve the moisture handling of this layer in the wall.

Hempcrete prefabricated wall - Life Cycle Inventory
Required processes:
Dimensions of functional unit:
No need of pesticides and herbicides, no need of irrigating water. All products from the plant are used and while growing per hectar of produced hempcrete, 21.6 ton CO2 are 
absorbed. source: [Luca Zampori, Giovanni Dotelli, and Valeria Vernelli. “Life Cycle Assessment of Hemp Cultivation and Use of Hemp Based Thermal Insulator Materials in 
Buildings”. (2013).] and [S. González-García, A. Hospido, M.T. Moreira and G. Feijoo, Life Cycle Environmental Analysis of Hemp Production for Non-wood Pulp, (2007)] ). 
bags of hemp shives (1 bag 200 L of 
mixture)
Each of this tables is the inventory of one required porcess to complete the whole wall system taken as fucntional unit. This processes are then inserted in the 
software Sima Pro to calculate the Global warming potential of the whole functional unit, as well as for each process taken singularly.

A.10
Material properties
254
Prefabricated wall element with hemp and bamboo
==PAGE:265==
GETTO
DESCRIZIONE
Calcecanapa® Getto è un biocomposto naturale, ecologico, di alta qualità a base di 
calce e canapa. E’ leggero, resistente ma ﬂessibile, naturalmente traspirante, capace 
di offrire elevato isolamento termo-acustico. Contribuisce efﬁcacemente a fornire un 
ambiente ad alto comfort abitativo, grazie alla sua leggerezza e soprattutto alle 
componenti di origine naturale. 
Calcecanapa® Getto determina uno sfasamento termico altamente efﬁciente: in 
estate il fresco accumulato dall’involucro nelle ore notturne è rilasciato all'interno 
degli ambienti con ritardo, attenuando il picco di calore. 
Calcecanapa® Getto non teme l’attacco di roditori ed insetti.
DESTINAZIONE 
D’USO
Calcecanapa® Getto si impiega sia nel recupero del costruito che nell’edilizia di 
nuova costruzione. 
E’ ideale per la realizzazione di contropareti isolanti su struttura esistente, da 
applicare con casseri (smontabili o a perdere), sia in interno sia in esterno. Si adatta 
perfettamente a tutte le superﬁci comunemente utilizzate in edilizia (laterizio, 
pietrame, cemento, legno, paglia, ecc.) svolgendo un’azione protettiva delle strutture.
Nelle nuove costruzioni viene utilizzato come tamponamento di chiusura nelle 
pareti perimetrali, per il miglioramento dell’efﬁcienza energetica e il naturale controllo 
dell'umidità.
COMPONENTI
•
Calce aerea magnesiaca  (DL 90-30 S-PL UNI EN 459-1:2010). Legante aereo 
che assicura lavorabilità e traspirabilità.
•
Canapulo mineralizzato. Aggregato leggero ad alto potere isolante.
MISCELAZIONE
Calcecanapa® Getto è un materiale pronto all’uso, non è necessaria alcuna 
miscelazione o aggiunta.
PREPARAZIONE 
DEL SUPPORTO
Nel caso in cui si operi su una struttura muraria esistente:
• Su superﬁci grezze (muratura in laterizio, pietra, ecc.), rimuovere l’intonaco pre-
esistente, parzialmente o totalmente, specie se tratta di intonaco cementizio, 
asportare polveri e parti fragili.
• Su superﬁcie lisce (murature cementizie, ecc.) applicare un rinzaffo a calce.
POSA IN OPERA
Per l’applicazione di Calcecanapa® Getto è necessario realizzare un’orditura lignea, 
capace di assicurare l’ancoraggio della miscela alla muratura, e un cassero di 
contenimento temporaneo o permanente.
Successivamente si applica a mano o a macchina in spessore da 10 a 40 cm.
Per dettagli consultare il Manuale di Posa.
Calcecanapa® Getto è ideale per contropareti e murature massive a 
base di calce e canapa 
ULTIMO AGGIORNAMENTO 17/04/2020
==PAGE:266==
GETTO
ULTIMO AGGIORNAMENTO 17/04/2020
INTONACI E 
FINITURE
In combinazione con Calcecanapa® Getto è consigliato l’utilizzo di Calcecanapa® 
Intonaco e Calcecanapa® Finitura, che costituisce una soluzione ad alte prestazioni 
termo-isolanti e ad alto valore estetico.
AVVERTENZE
Applicare con temperature comprese tra +5°C e +30°C.
Calcecanapa® Getto deve essere separato dai piani di calpestio (ove possano 
veriﬁcarsi ristagni d'acqua e dal contatto con il terreno (al ﬁne d’evitare l’innesco del 
fenomeno di risalita capillare d’acqua.

==PAGE:267==
PAN80
ULTIMO AGGIORNAMENTO 20/12/19
DESCRIZIONE
Calcecanapa® PAN 80 è una lastra d’isolamento in ﬁbra di canapa caratterizzata da 
un eccellente valore di conducibilità termica ed elevata resistenza meccanica. La sua 
capacità d’isolamento termico-acustico è la stessa dei più comuni materiali isolanti, 
con il vantaggio di un prodotto naturale e traspirante.
Calcecanapa® PAN80 ha una capacità termica doppia rispetto ai normali isolanti 
minerali (C= 1.700 J/Kg K) pertanto l’ediﬁcio isolato si raffredda-scalda molto meno 
intensamente, con vantaggi evidentissimi in termini di comfort estivo/invernale.
Oltre il potere termoisolante, la caratteristica principale della ﬁbra di canapa sono la 
traspirabilità e la capacità di assorbire e rilasciare l’umidità. 
Da ciò, un salutare microclima nell'ambiente domestico, senza formazione muffe e 
batteri, causa di allergie e altri disturbi respiratori. 
La canapa è un materiale isolante straordinario, anche elevata capacità di 
assorbimento di umidità e condensa. La canapa mantiene la propria forma anche in 
condizioni di elevata umidità: non s’imbarca e non perde le sue proprietà isolanti.
Le caratteristiche di Calcecanapa® PAN80 sono apprezzate da chi vive in vie 
frequentate o vicino a strade molto trafﬁcate. Il suo isolamento acustico offre, infatti, 
protezione su qualsiasi tipo di pareti, per tutti gli ediﬁci, sia moderni sia storici. 
Calcecanapa® PAN80 garantisce piena libertà in termini di design e colore: la 
facciata può essere ﬁnita anche con colori molto scuri e le superﬁcie 
signiﬁcativamente materiche e strutturate. 
DESTINAZIONE 
D’USO
Ideale per l’isolamento esterno ed interno dei muri perimetrali per costruzioni di 
nuova realizzazione e il restauro di ediﬁci esistenti in muratura, calcestruzzo e 
legno.
POSA IN OPERA
Le superﬁci del supporto devono essere pulite e coese, in caso contrario si dovrà 
procedere alla rimozione di polvere e sporco, parti sfarinanti ed in distacco, ecc. 
E’ consigliato realizzare uno zoccolo di partenza per non esporre i pannelli all’umidità 
del terreno e garantire una corretta tenuta inferiore dei pannelli isolanti.
Il ﬁssaggio avviene tramite colla/rasante Calcecanapa® PanGlue e tasselli ad 
espansione. Gli spessori disponibili e la possibilità di accoppiare tra lori i pannelli, 
permettono una scelta versatile, in base alle esigenze d’isolamento termico e in 
osservanza alla legislazione vigente.
Per dettagli consultare il Manuale di Posa.
Calcecanapa® PAN80 è una lastra da isolamento termo-acustico in 
ﬁbra di canapa, ideale per interni ed esterni.

A.12
Adjusted project plan
Prefabricated wall element with hemp and bamboo

==PAGE:270==
Elsa Maria Iuliano & Helena Brandt Rejndrup 
UPDATED MASTER THESIS PROJECT PLAN  
Thesis title 
Design and assessment of a prefabricated wall element made out of the sustainable 
materials hemp and bamboo 
Thesis description 
It is not very common to consider the building sector as one of the main actors in climate change, even 
though it emits 35% of the greenhouse gases in Europe. Although it is getting more popular to develop 
solutions with alternative low impacting materials to tackle this issue. Hemp and bamboo stand out 
due to their valuable properties, both are sustainable due to fast growth and low maintenance as well 
as having competitive structural and thermal properties. 
The aim of this Thesis is to design an alternative building solution which can compete with the existing 
ones, but have a smaller carbon footprint. A prefabricated element made out of bamboo and hemp is 
designed. The element is designed to be economically affordable, build-able and standardized, as well 
as fulfil the requirements of the building regulation. 
The project includes the assessment of how the materials can be used and the different ways to 
combine them, which leads to design phase where the prefabricated wall element is developed based 
on evaluations of the different combinations. Afterwards the build-ability of the element in a 
construction is studied, this phase is combined with the creation of prototype in the lab. Finally the 
technical properties and the sustainability parameters of the final design are assessed and compared 
to traditional construction ways. 
Learning objectives 
The process of this Master Thesis will follow Bloom’s Taxonomy pyramid, this means that theoretical knowledge 
will be the base of the work, its analysis and synthesis will be translated in a design, which finally will be tested 
and evaluated. The following learning objectives summarize both the process and the performance of the master 
Thesis: 
1. Collect enough knowledge about the researched materials and their properties, to be able to conclude 
which material use performs better than others. 
2. Collect enough knowledge about the construction industry, to analyse the possibility of substituting 
less sustainable materials with the developed prefabricated element. 
3. Defining the issues and needs in the construction industry. 
4. Design and evaluation of different design concepts to outline the best performing option 
5. Design of a prefabricated element based on the issues and needs of the construction industry. 
6. Create a prototype, to evaluate the cohesiveness of the materials and the practical aspects of the 
designed element. 
7. Analysis and interpretation of the developed results and knowledge. 
8. Evaluation of the design details, such as structural layout, joints and connections, as well as 
manufacturing, buildability, transportability, installation. 
9. Evaluation of final design, for its technical and economical performances as well as how it tackles the 
environmental  issues in the industry. 
10. Development of a state-of-the-art thesis report, which documents the design process as well as the 
results of the different research subjects. 
260
